#### 10.3c Future of Zoos and Animal Exhibits

As we delve into the future of zoos and animal exhibits, it is important to consider the ethical debates surrounding these institutions. The future of zoos and animal exhibits is not just about physical expansion or technological advancements, but also about addressing the ethical concerns that have been raised.

##### The Role of Technology

Technology has the potential to play a significant role in the future of zoos and animal exhibits. Advancements in technology can be used to improve the quality of life for animals in captivity. For instance, the use of virtual reality technology can provide animals with simulated natural environments, allowing them to engage in natural behaviors that they would not be able to do in a traditional zoo setting.

However, technology can also be a double-edged sword. While it can improve the welfare of animals, it can also be used to further confine and control animals. For example, the use of advanced surveillance systems can allow zoos to monitor animals more closely, potentially limiting their freedom and natural behaviors.

##### The Importance of Public Education

Public education is another crucial aspect of the future of zoos and animal exhibits. Zoos have the potential to serve as powerful educational tools, teaching the public about the natural world and the importance of conservation. However, this potential can only be realized if zoos are willing to engage in honest and transparent discussions about the ethical issues surrounding their existence.

In the future, zoos will need to be more transparent about their operations, including their breeding programs and veterinary care. They will also need to be more proactive in addressing the ethical concerns raised by animal rights activists. This could include implementing more comprehensive enrichment programs, expanding their veterinary facilities, and investing in research to better understand the needs and behaviors of the animals in their care.

##### The Need for Sustainability

Finally, the future of zoos and animal exhibits will need to be sustainable. This means not only ensuring the welfare of the animals in their care, but also minimizing their impact on the environment. Zoos can achieve this by implementing sustainable practices, such as using renewable energy sources and reducing their carbon footprint. They can also work towards preserving natural habitats and supporting conservation efforts in the wild.

In conclusion, the future of zoos and animal exhibits is not just about physical expansion or technological advancements. It is about addressing the ethical concerns surrounding these institutions and working towards a more sustainable and transparent future.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the history and evolution of zoos in American urban spaces. We have seen how zoos have transformed from private menageries to public institutions, and how they have played a significant role in shaping our understanding of nature and wildlife. We have also delved into the ethical debates surrounding zoos, particularly in terms of animal welfare and conservation.

Zoos have been instrumental in preserving endangered species and educating the public about wildlife. However, they have also been criticized for their confinement of animals and the potential for exploitation. As we move forward, it is crucial to continue exploring these debates and finding ways to balance the benefits of zoos with the ethical concerns they raise.

The future of zoos in American urban spaces is uncertain, but it is clear that they will continue to play a significant role in our relationship with nature. As we continue to urbanize and our connection with the natural world becomes increasingly tenuous, zoos may become even more important as spaces for learning and appreciation of wildlife.

## Chapter: Chapter 11: The American Dream

### Introduction

The American Dream, a concept deeply ingrained in the fabric of American society, has been a driving force behind the growth and development of American cities. This chapter will delve into the exploration of the American Dream in the context of urban history, examining how it has shaped the urban landscape and the lives of Americans.

The American Dream, a concept that has been variously defined and interpreted, is often associated with the idea of upward mobility, the opportunity for individuals to improve their social and economic status. It is a dream that has been both a source of inspiration and a cause of conflict in American society. This chapter will explore the historical context of the American Dream, tracing its origins and evolution, and examining its impact on urban spaces.

In the realm of urban history, the American Dream has played a significant role in shaping the physical and social landscape of American cities. It has influenced the design and development of urban spaces, the distribution of resources, and the social and economic dynamics within cities. This chapter will delve into these aspects, providing a comprehensive exploration of the American Dream in urban history.

The American Dream is not just a concept, but a lived experience for many Americans. This chapter will also explore the lived experiences of Americans in relation to the American Dream, examining how the concept has shaped their lives and their relationship with urban spaces.

In exploring the American Dream, this chapter aims to provide a nuanced understanding of this concept in the context of urban history. It seeks to shed light on the complexities and contradictions of the American Dream, and its profound impact on American cities and the lives of Americans.




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the history and evolution of zoos in America. From their early beginnings as menageries and private collections, to their transformation into public institutions dedicated to conservation and education, zoos have played a significant role in shaping American urban history.

The first zoos in America were established in the late 18th and early 19th centuries, often as private collections of exotic animals owned by wealthy individuals. These menageries were popular attractions for the public, who were fascinated by the exotic creatures on display. However, these early zoos were often cruel and inhumane, with animals being kept in cramped and unsanitary conditions.

As the 19th century progressed, there was a growing movement towards the establishment of public zoos, with the goal of providing a more educational and humane experience for both the animals and the public. This led to the creation of the first public zoo in America, the Philadelphia Zoo, in 1874.

The 20th century saw a significant shift in the role of zoos, with a focus on conservation and education. Zoos became important centers for research and breeding programs, working to preserve endangered species and educate the public about the importance of conservation. This shift was driven by advancements in technology and veterinary medicine, which allowed for better care and treatment of animals.

Today, zoos continue to play a crucial role in American urban history, serving as important cultural and educational institutions. They provide a unique opportunity for the public to interact with and learn about wildlife, while also contributing to conservation efforts. As we continue to grow and evolve as a society, zoos will undoubtedly play a vital role in shaping the future of American cities.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the history and evolution of zoos in America. From their early beginnings as menageries and private collections, to their transformation into public institutions dedicated to conservation and education, zoos have played a significant role in shaping American urban history.

The first zoos in America were established in the late 18th and early 19th centuries, often as private collections of exotic animals owned by wealthy individuals. These menageries were popular attractions for the public, who were fascinated by the exotic creatures on display. However, these early zoos were often cruel and inhumane, with animals being kept in cramped and unsanitary conditions.

As the 19th century progressed, there was a growing movement towards the establishment of public zoos, with the goal of providing a more educational and humane experience for both the animals and the public. This led to the creation of the first public zoo in America, the Philadelphia Zoo, in 1874.

The 20th century saw a significant shift in the role of zoos, with a focus on conservation and education. Zoos became important centers for research and breeding programs, working to preserve endangered species and educate the public about the importance of conservation. This shift was driven by advancements in technology and veterinary medicine, which allowed for better care and treatment of animals.

Today, zoos continue to play a crucial role in American urban history, serving as important cultural and educational institutions. They provide a unique opportunity for the public to interact with and learn about wildlife, while also contributing to conservation efforts. As we continue to grow and evolve as a society, zoos will undoubtedly play a vital role in shaping the future of American cities.

## Chapter: American Urban History II: Exploring the Growth of American Cities

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the topic of urban planning in America. Urban planning is a crucial aspect of city development and management, as it involves the design and organization of the physical environment of a city. It is a multidisciplinary field that combines elements of architecture, landscape architecture, urban design, and social sciences to create functional and aesthetically pleasing cities.

The history of urban planning in America dates back to the early 19th century, when the first cities were being established. As the population grew and cities expanded, the need for organized and efficient planning became apparent. This led to the development of various urban planning theories and techniques, which have been continuously evolving to address the changing needs and challenges of American cities.

In this chapter, we will explore the evolution of urban planning in America, from its early beginnings to the present day. We will examine the key factors that have influenced urban planning, such as population growth, economic development, and social and cultural changes. We will also discuss the various approaches and techniques used in urban planning, including zoning, transportation planning, and public participation.

Furthermore, we will examine the impact of urban planning on the growth and development of American cities. We will look at how urban planning has shaped the physical and social characteristics of cities, and how it has influenced the quality of life for residents. We will also discuss the challenges and controversies surrounding urban planning, such as gentrification, inequality, and sustainability.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of urban planning in America, its history, principles, and impact. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a deeper appreciation for the complex and ever-evolving field of urban planning and its role in shaping the cities we live in.


# American Urban History II: Exploring the Growth of American Cities

## Chapter 11: Urban Planning




### Introduction

Cemeteries have played a significant role in the history of American cities. They have served as more than just a final resting place for the deceased, but also as a reflection of the cultural, social, and religious values of the communities they serve. In this chapter, we will explore the history of cemeteries in American cities, from their early beginnings to the present day. We will examine how cemeteries have evolved over time, the various types of cemeteries that exist, and the impact they have had on the growth and development of American cities.

Cemeteries have been a part of human society since ancient times, and their purpose has evolved over the centuries. In the early days of American settlement, cemeteries were often located on church grounds or in remote areas outside of town. However, as cities began to grow and expand, the need for more accessible and organized burial grounds became apparent. This led to the establishment of municipal cemeteries, which were often designed with grandiose architecture and landscaping to reflect the wealth and power of the city.

As the population continued to grow, the demand for more space in cemeteries also increased. This led to the development of new types of cemeteries, such as garden cemeteries and memorial parks. These cemeteries were designed to be more natural and serene, providing a peaceful resting place for the deceased.

In addition to their role as a final resting place, cemeteries have also been used as a means of preserving history. Many cemeteries contain tombstones and monuments that provide valuable information about the people who lived in the city during a particular time period. This information can be used to gain insight into the cultural, social, and religious practices of the time.

In this chapter, we will delve into the history of cemeteries in American cities, exploring their evolution, types, and impact. We will also examine the role of cemeteries in preserving history and how they have shaped the growth and development of American cities. 





### Subsection: 11.1a Early Cemeteries and Burial Grounds

The history of cemeteries in America dates back to the early days of settlement, when burial grounds were often located on church grounds or in remote areas outside of town. These early cemeteries were simple and unadorned, reflecting the modest lifestyle of the early settlers. However, as cities began to grow and expand, the need for more accessible and organized burial grounds became apparent.

One of the earliest recorded instances of post-Anglo-Saxon people excavating an early Anglo-Saxon burial comes from the 12th century, when Roger of Wendover described how several monks dug up the burial mounds at Redbourne, Hertfordshire, in search of the bones of Saint Amphibalus, a Roman period priest. This early excavation was driven by a desire for religious relics, a common practice during this time period.

In the 17th century, Sir Thomas Browne published a pamphlet entitled "Hydrotaphia, Urn Burial" (1658), in which he described a number of cremation urns found in Norfolk. Despite these earlier excavations, it was not until the 18th century that archaeologists began to systematically excavate and study Anglo-Saxon cemeteries.

The accolade of being the first excavators of Anglo-Saxon cemeteries should really go to two Kentish gentlemen clerics: the antiquarian Reverend Bryan Faussett and James Douglas. Between 1759 and 1773, Faussett excavated at a number of cemeteries in Kent, including Gilton, Kingstone Down, Chartham Down, and Sibertswold. Uncovering about 750 graves, he made detailed records in his field notebooks noting anatomical details, but like Browne before him, he mistakenly attributed them to Roman-Britain.

Following his death in 1776, Faussett's notes were written up and published in 1856 as the "Inventorium Sepulchrale" by Charles Roach Smith, who added his own commentary to the work. Douglas, on the other hand, published his findings in a book entitled "Nenia Britannica" (1793). These early excavations not only provided valuable insights into the lives of early Anglo-Saxon settlers, but also laid the foundation for the modern field of archaeology.

In the next section, we will explore the evolution of cemetery design and landscape architecture, from the simple and unadorned burial grounds of early settlers to the grand and ornate cemeteries of the 19th and 20th centuries.





### Subsection: 11.1b Cemeteries and Landscape Design

As cities continued to grow and expand, the need for more organized and aesthetically pleasing burial grounds became increasingly apparent. This led to the development of landscape architecture as a means of designing and shaping the physical environment to create a sense of order and beauty. In the context of cemeteries, landscape architecture played a crucial role in transforming these spaces from simple burial grounds to serene and peaceful landscapes.

One of the earliest examples of landscape architecture in cemeteries can be seen in the work of the renowned landscape architect Frederick Law Olmsted. Olmsted, who is best known for his design of New York's Central Park, also played a significant role in shaping the landscape of cemeteries. His design for Mount Auburn Cemetery in Cambridge, Massachusetts, is considered a masterpiece of landscape architecture. Olmsted's design incorporated natural elements such as winding paths, rolling hills, and native plants to create a picturesque and serene landscape. This approach not only enhanced the aesthetic appeal of the cemetery but also provided a sense of tranquility and solitude for visitors.

The influence of Olmsted's work can be seen in the design of many other cemeteries, including Green-Wood Cemetery in Brooklyn, New York, and Woodlawn Cemetery in The Bronx, New York. These cemeteries, like Mount Auburn, incorporate natural elements and landscape design to create a sense of order and beauty. The use of landscape architecture in cemeteries not only enhances the aesthetic appeal of these spaces but also serves as a means of memorialization, allowing visitors to connect with the deceased in a more meaningful way.

In addition to its aesthetic and memorial functions, landscape architecture also plays a crucial role in the preservation of cemeteries. As cities continue to grow and expand, cemeteries are often faced with the challenge of limited space. Landscape architecture can help address this issue by creating more efficient and organized layouts, allowing for the burial of more individuals in a given space. Furthermore, the use of native plants and sustainable design practices can help preserve the natural environment surrounding the cemetery.

In conclusion, landscape architecture has played a significant role in the evolution of cemetery design. From creating serene and picturesque landscapes to addressing issues of space and preservation, landscape architecture has helped transform cemeteries from simple burial grounds to meaningful and aesthetically pleasing spaces. As cities continue to grow and evolve, the role of landscape architecture in cemetery design will only become more crucial.





### Subsection: 11.1c Cemeteries and Urban Green Spaces

Cemeteries have long been a part of urban landscapes, serving as both a place of rest for the deceased and a green space for the living. As cities continue to grow and expand, the role of cemeteries in urban green spaces has become increasingly important.

One of the key benefits of cemeteries as urban green spaces is their ability to provide a sense of tranquility and solitude in the midst of a bustling city. As mentioned in the previous section, the design of cemeteries often incorporates natural elements such as winding paths, rolling hills, and native plants, creating a serene and peaceful environment. This is especially important in urban areas where green spaces are often scarce and the noise and chaos of city life can be overwhelming.

Moreover, cemeteries also serve as a valuable resource for urban ecology. As mentioned in the related context, cemeteries can provide important habitats for a variety of species, including birds, butterflies, and other wildlife. In fact, some cemeteries have been designated as wildlife sanctuaries due to their importance in preserving biodiversity. This is particularly significant in urban areas where natural habitats are often destroyed or fragmented by development.

In addition to their ecological benefits, cemeteries also play a crucial role in the social and cultural life of urban communities. They serve as gathering places for families and friends to pay their respects to loved ones, and can also be sites for community events and celebrations. This is especially true in ethnically diverse urban areas, where cemeteries can serve as cultural hubs, preserving traditions and customs related to death and mourning.

However, the use of cemeteries as urban green spaces is not without its challenges. As mentioned in the previous section, the limited space in urban areas can make it difficult to expand or maintain cemeteries. This is especially true in older cities where cemeteries may be located in densely populated areas. Additionally, the increasing popularity of cremation and the rise of urban densification have also led to a decrease in the demand for traditional burial plots, further complicating the issue.

Despite these challenges, the importance of cemeteries as urban green spaces cannot be overlooked. As cities continue to grow and evolve, it is crucial to find ways to preserve and enhance these spaces, not only for the benefit of the deceased, but also for the living. This can be achieved through innovative design and landscape architecture, as well as through community engagement and support. By recognizing the value of cemeteries as urban green spaces, we can ensure their continued existence and contribution to the overall well-being of our cities.





### Subsection: 11.2a Cemeteries as Social Spaces

Cemeteries have long been a part of urban landscapes, serving as both a place of rest for the deceased and a social space for the living. As cities continue to grow and evolve, the role of cemeteries in urban society has become increasingly complex.

#### The Social Significance of Cemeteries

Cemeteries have been a part of human society since ancient times, serving as a place for the dead to rest and a site for communal mourning and remembrance. In urban areas, cemeteries have taken on a unique role as a social space, where people can gather to pay their respects, reflect on their own mortality, and connect with their community.

The design of cemeteries often reflects the values and beliefs of the society in which they exist. For example, in the United States, the rise of the middle class in the 19th century led to a shift in cemetery design from the crowded, chaotic churchyards of the past to more orderly, landscaped cemeteries. This reflected the desire for order and control in the face of death, as well as the growing importance of individualism and personal expression.

#### Cemeteries as Cultural Hubs

In addition to their role as a social space, cemeteries also serve as cultural hubs in urban areas. They are often sites of cultural and religious traditions, such as Da de los Muertos in Mexico or Tomb Sweeping Day in China. These traditions allow communities to come together and honor their deceased loved ones, while also preserving their cultural identity.

Furthermore, cemeteries can also serve as a place for intergenerational learning and transmission of cultural values. For example, in many Asian cultures, children are often brought to cemeteries to learn about their ancestors and the importance of respecting the dead. This not only helps to preserve cultural traditions, but also fosters a sense of community and belonging.

#### Challenges and Opportunities

Despite their social and cultural significance, cemeteries face numerous challenges in urban areas. Limited space and resources, as well as increasing urbanization, make it difficult to maintain and expand cemeteries. This has led to the development of innovative solutions, such as vertical cemeteries and green burials, which aim to address these challenges while still preserving the social and cultural importance of cemeteries.

In addition, the use of cemeteries as social spaces has also led to the development of new forms of memorialization, such as living memorials and digital memorials. These allow for a more personal and interactive way of remembering and honoring the dead, while also addressing the limitations of traditional cemeteries.

### Conclusion

Cemeteries have played a significant role in urban society throughout history, serving as a place of rest for the deceased and a social space for the living. As cities continue to evolve, so too will the role of cemeteries, adapting to new challenges and opportunities while still preserving their social and cultural significance. 





### Subsection: 11.2b Cemeteries and Cultural Heritage

Cemeteries are not only a place of rest for the deceased, but also a reflection of the cultural heritage of a community. The design, layout, and traditions surrounding cemeteries can provide valuable insights into the history, beliefs, and values of a society.

#### Cemeteries as Cultural Heritage

Cemeteries are an important part of our cultural heritage, representing the beliefs, values, and traditions of a community. They are a physical manifestation of our relationship with death and the afterlife, and can provide a deeper understanding of our cultural identity.

The design of cemeteries can vary greatly depending on the cultural and religious background of a community. For example, in the United States, the rise of the middle class in the 19th century led to a shift in cemetery design from the crowded, chaotic churchyards of the past to more orderly, landscaped cemeteries. This reflects the desire for order and control in the face of death, as well as the growing importance of individualism and personal expression.

#### Cemeteries as Sites of Cultural Traditions

Cemeteries are also sites of cultural traditions, where communities come together to honor their deceased loved ones. These traditions can vary greatly depending on the cultural and religious background of a community. For example, in Mexico, the Day of the Dead is a popular tradition where families visit the graves of their loved ones and leave offerings of food and drink. In China, Tomb Sweeping Day is a traditional festival where families clean and offer sacrifices to their ancestors.

These traditions not only allow communities to come together and honor their deceased loved ones, but also preserve cultural values and beliefs. For example, the Day of the Dead tradition in Mexico emphasizes the belief in the afterlife and the idea of a continuity of life after death. Tomb Sweeping Day in China, on the other hand, highlights the importance of filial piety and respect for one's ancestors.

#### Cemeteries as Cultural Hubs

Cemeteries also serve as cultural hubs, where communities gather to learn about their cultural heritage and traditions. For example, in many Asian cultures, children are brought to cemeteries to learn about their ancestors and the importance of respecting the dead. This not only helps to preserve cultural traditions, but also fosters a sense of community and belonging.

In conclusion, cemeteries are not just a place of rest for the deceased, but also a reflection of our cultural heritage and a site of cultural traditions. They play a crucial role in shaping our understanding of death and the afterlife, and serve as a reminder of our shared cultural identity. 





### Subsection: 11.2c Cemeteries and Community Identity

Cemeteries not only reflect the cultural heritage and traditions of a community, but also play a crucial role in shaping community identity. The design, layout, and traditions surrounding cemeteries can provide a deeper understanding of the values, beliefs, and history of a community.

#### Cemeteries as Reflections of Community Identity

Cemeteries are a physical manifestation of a community's identity. They are a place where the community comes together to honor its deceased members and remember their contributions to the community. The design and layout of a cemetery can reflect the social, cultural, and economic status of the community. For example, in the United States, the rise of the middle class in the 19th century led to a shift in cemetery design from the crowded, chaotic churchyards of the past to more orderly, landscaped cemeteries. This shift reflects the growing importance of individualism and personal expression in American society.

#### Cemeteries as Sites of Community Memory

Cemeteries are also sites of community memory, where the community remembers and honors its deceased members. The traditions and rituals surrounding cemeteries can vary greatly depending on the cultural and religious background of a community. For example, in the United States, Memorial Day is a national holiday that honors the men and women who died while serving in the military. This tradition reflects the community's respect for its veterans and their sacrifice for the country.

#### Cemeteries as Places of Community Gathering

Cemeteries are also places of community gathering, where people come together to remember and honor their deceased loved ones. This can be seen in the tradition of graveyard picnics, where families gather at the graves of their loved ones to share food, stories, and memories. This tradition reflects the community's sense of togetherness and support in the face of loss.

In conclusion, cemeteries play a crucial role in shaping community identity. They are a reflection of the community's cultural heritage, traditions, and values. They are also sites of community memory and gathering, where the community comes together to honor its deceased members. Understanding the social and cultural significance of cemeteries is essential in exploring the growth of American cities.





### Subsection: 11.3a Traditional Funeral Practices

Traditional funeral practices have been an integral part of human culture for thousands of years. These practices are deeply rooted in cultural, religious, and social beliefs, and they serve to honor the deceased and comfort the living. In this section, we will explore the traditional funeral practices of the Ojibwe people, a Native American tribe.

#### Ojibwe Funeral Practices: Traditional

The Ojibwe people have a rich history of funeral practices that are deeply intertwined with their spiritual beliefs. The main task after a death is to bury the body as soon as possible, typically within the next day or even on the day of death. This is important because it allows the spirit of the dead to journey to its place of joy and happiness, known as "Gaagige Minawaanigozigiwining". This journey takes four days, and during this time, the body is placed in an inflexed position with their knees towards their chest.

The Ojibwe believe that food and a fire are necessary for the spirit's journey. A fire is set when the sun sets and is kept going throughout the night. The food is to help feed the spirit over the course of the journey, while the smoke from the fire is a directional guide. Once the four day journey is over, a feast is held, which is led by the chief medicine man. At the feast, it is the chief medicine man's duty to give away certain belongings of the deceased. Those who were chosen to receive items from the deceased are required to trade in a new piece of clothing, all of which would be turned into a bundle. The bundle of new cloths and a dish is then given to the closest relative. The recipient of the bundle must then find individuals that he or she believes to be worthy, and pass on one of the new pieces of clothing.

#### Ojibwe Funeral Practices: Contemporary

While contemporary Ojibwe funeral practices may vary slightly from traditional practices, they still follow the same spiritual beliefs. According to Lee Staples, an Ojibwe spiritual leader from the Mille Lacs Indian Reservation, present day practices involve the same four day journey for the spirit, with the body being placed in an inflexed position and a fire being lit to guide the spirit. However, contemporary practices may also include the use of modern technology, such as embalming and cremation, which were not available to the Ojibwe people in the past.

In conclusion, traditional funeral practices of the Ojibwe people are deeply rooted in their spiritual beliefs and serve to honor the deceased and comfort the living. While contemporary practices may vary slightly, they still uphold the same spiritual beliefs and traditions.

### Subsection: 11.3b Changing Funeral Practices

As societies evolve, so do their funeral practices. The Ojibwe people, like many other cultures, have seen a shift in their funeral practices over time. This shift has been largely influenced by cultural exchange, technological advancements, and changes in religious beliefs.

#### Ojibwe Funeral Practices: Modern

In modern times, the Ojibwe people have adopted some elements of Western funeral practices, such as embalming and cremation. Embalming, the process of preserving a body for viewing and burial, was not a part of traditional Ojibwe funeral practices. However, with the introduction of modern technology and the rise of funeral homes, embalming has become a common practice among the Ojibwe people.

Cremation, on the other hand, has become increasingly popular among the Ojibwe people. This practice, which involves burning the body to ashes, was not traditionally part of Ojibwe funeral practices. However, with the rise of urbanization and the increasing cost of burial plots, cremation has become a more affordable and practical option for many Ojibwe families.

#### The Rise of Cremation

The rise of cremation in the United States can be traced back to the late 19th century, when it was first introduced by the Catholic Church as an alternative to burial during the cholera epidemic. Since then, cremation rates have been steadily increasing, with 50% of Americans now choosing cremation over traditional burial.

The rise of cremation has been influenced by a variety of factors, including cultural exchange, technological advancements, and changes in religious beliefs. For example, the introduction of cremation to the Ojibwe people has been influenced by their interactions with other cultures, as well as the availability of modern technology.

#### The Environmental Impact of Cremation

While cremation has become a popular option for many Americans, it is not without its environmental impact. Cremation involves burning a body at high temperatures, which releases pollutants into the atmosphere. These pollutants can have negative effects on the environment, including contributing to air pollution and climate change.

In response to these concerns, some funeral homes have begun offering "green" or "eco-friendly" cremation services. These services aim to reduce the environmental impact of cremation by using alternative fuels, such as liquid nitrogen, and by recycling the remains into useful products, such as fertilizer or concrete.

#### The Future of Funeral Practices

As societies continue to evolve, so will their funeral practices. With the rise of urbanization and the increasing cost of burial plots, it is likely that cremation rates will continue to rise. However, as the environmental impact of cremation becomes a greater concern, there may be a shift towards more sustainable funeral practices.

Furthermore, advancements in technology may also play a role in shaping future funeral practices. For example, the development of new technologies, such as body freezing or digital funerals, could provide alternative options to traditional burial and cremation.

In conclusion, the changing funeral practices of the Ojibwe people and the rise of cremation in the United States highlight the dynamic nature of funeral practices. As societies continue to evolve, so will their funeral practices, reflecting the cultural, religious, and environmental concerns of the time.

### Subsection: 11.3c Cemeteries and Changing Funeral Practices

The changing funeral practices of the Ojibwe people have also had a significant impact on cemeteries. As the use of embalming and cremation has become more prevalent, the traditional methods of burial have become less common. This has led to a shift in the way cemeteries are designed and maintained.

#### The Evolution of Cemeteries

Historically, cemeteries were designed as sacred spaces for the burial of the dead. They were often located outside of urban areas, in natural settings such as forests or valleys. The Ojibwe people, like many other cultures, had specific rituals and traditions surrounding burial, which were reflected in the design of their cemeteries.

However, with the rise of urbanization and the increasing use of embalming and cremation, cemeteries have become more integrated into urban landscapes. Many cemeteries now have modern facilities, such as funeral homes and mausoleums, and are designed to accommodate a variety of funeral practices.

#### The Impact of Changing Funeral Practices

The changing funeral practices of the Ojibwe people have also had a significant impact on the management of cemeteries. With the rise of embalming, cemeteries now have to deal with the storage and disposal of embalming fluids, which can be hazardous to the environment.

Cremation has also led to changes in cemetery management. As cremation becomes more popular, there is a growing need for crematoriums and columbariums, which are used to store and display cremated remains. This has led to the development of new cemetery designs, such as "green" or "eco-friendly" cemeteries, which aim to reduce the environmental impact of cremation.

#### The Future of Cemeteries

As funeral practices continue to evolve, so will the design and management of cemeteries. With the rise of digital technology, there has been a growing trend towards digital funerals, where the funeral service is streamed online. This could lead to a shift in the way cemeteries are designed, with more emphasis on digital memorials and less on traditional burial plots.

Furthermore, as the population continues to grow and urban areas become more densely populated, there may be a need for more innovative solutions for managing cemeteries. This could include the use of vertical cemeteries, where graves are stacked in layers, or the development of new technologies for the storage and disposal of remains.

In conclusion, the changing funeral practices of the Ojibwe people have had a significant impact on cemeteries. As societies continue to evolve, so will their funeral practices, and this will inevitably shape the future of cemeteries.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the history and evolution of cemeteries in American urban areas. We have seen how these spaces have transformed over time, from simple burial grounds to elaborate and ornate cemeteries, reflecting the changing values and beliefs of society. We have also examined the role of cemeteries in the urban landscape, and how they have influenced the development of cities.

From the earliest days of colonial America, when cemeteries were often located outside of town, to the modern era where they are often found within city limits, we have seen how cemeteries have adapted to the changing needs and demands of urban populations. We have also discussed the impact of urbanization on cemeteries, and how the growth of cities has led to the consolidation and expansion of cemeteries.

Furthermore, we have delved into the cultural and social significance of cemeteries, and how they have been used as a reflection of the values and beliefs of different communities. From the grand and ornate cemeteries of the Victorian era, to the more modest and functional cemeteries of today, we have seen how these spaces have evolved to meet the needs and desires of the people who use them.

In conclusion, cemeteries have played a crucial role in the development of American urban areas, and their history and evolution provide valuable insights into the growth and transformation of cities. As we continue to explore the urban landscape, it is important to remember the significance of these spaces and the stories they hold.

## Chapter: Chapter 12: The City and the Law

### Introduction

The city is a complex and dynamic entity, constantly evolving and adapting to the needs and desires of its inhabitants. As urban populations continue to grow, the challenges and complexities of city planning and management become increasingly apparent. In this chapter, we will delve into the intricate relationship between the city and the law, exploring how legal frameworks and regulations shape and influence urban development.

The city and the law are intertwined in a complex dance of regulation and innovation. The law provides the framework within which cities operate, setting the rules for land use, development, and public safety. However, the city also has the power to shape and influence the law, through its lobbying efforts and its role as a laboratory for innovative urban solutions.

In this chapter, we will explore the various legal aspects of urban development, including zoning laws, building codes, and environmental regulations. We will also examine the role of the city in shaping these laws, and the challenges and opportunities that this relationship presents.

As we navigate through the complexities of the city and the law, we will also consider the broader implications of these issues. How do these legal frameworks impact the lives of urban dwellers? How do they shape the character and identity of a city? And how do they influence the trajectory of urban development?

This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the city and the law, shedding light on the intricate relationship between these two entities. By the end of this chapter, readers should have a solid understanding of the legal aspects of urban development, and be equipped with the knowledge to navigate the complexities of the city and the law.




### Subsection: 11.3b Rise of Cremation

Cremation has been a widely accepted practice in many cultures around the world, including the United States. It is a process of reducing the body to bone fragments through the use of high temperatures. The practice of cremation has been traced back to ancient civilizations such as the Egyptians, who believed that it was a means of preserving the body for the afterlife. However, it was not until the 19th century that cremation became a popular alternative to traditional burial in the United States.

#### The History of Cremation in the United States

The first recorded cremation in the United States took place in 1876, when a man named Thomas P. Smith was cremated in a makeshift crematorium in New York City. However, it was not until the late 19th century that cremation became a widely accepted practice. The first crematorium in the United States was established in 1876 in Washington, D.C., and was operated by the Washington Crematory Company.

#### The Rise of Cremation in the 20th Century

The 20th century saw a significant increase in the popularity of cremation in the United States. This was largely due to the changing attitudes towards death and the growing acceptance of cremation as a more environmentally friendly and cost-effective alternative to traditional burial. In 1902, the Cremation Act was passed in the United Kingdom, which allowed for the legalization of cremation in England. This act also set the stage for the establishment of the Cremation Society of Great Britain, which played a crucial role in promoting and regulating cremation practices in the UK.

#### The Cremation Society of Great Britain and Its Impact on Cremation in the United States

The Cremation Society of Great Britain, founded in 1874, played a significant role in the rise of cremation in the United States. The society was instrumental in promoting and regulating cremation practices in the UK, and its efforts were not unnoticed by Americans. In 1876, the society established the Washington Crematory Company, which was the first crematorium in the United States. The society also played a crucial role in lobbying for the Cremation Act of 1902, which legalized cremation in England.

#### The Impact of Cremation on Cemetery Practices

The rise of cremation has had a significant impact on cemetery practices in the United States. With the increasing popularity of cremation, many cemeteries have had to adapt to accommodate the growing number of cremated remains. This has led to the development of new types of burial plots, such as columbariums, which are specifically designed for the interment of cremated remains. Cemeteries have also had to implement new policies and regulations to address the proper handling and storage of cremated remains.

#### The Future of Cremation in the United States

As the population continues to grow and the demand for burial space decreases, it is likely that cremation will become an even more popular alternative to traditional burial. With the advancements in technology and the increasing acceptance of cremation, it is likely that cremation will continue to rise in popularity in the United States.

### Conclusion

The rise of cremation in the United States has been a significant development in the history of funeral practices. From its early beginnings in ancient civilizations to its widespread acceptance in modern times, cremation has become a popular alternative to traditional burial. The impact of cremation on cemetery practices has been significant, and it is likely that cremation will continue to shape the future of funeral practices in the United States.





### Subsection: 11.3c Future of Funeral Practices

As we have seen in the previous sections, funeral practices have evolved significantly over time. From the ancient Egyptian practice of mummification to the modern trend of cremation, funeral practices have been shaped by cultural, religious, and societal influences. In this section, we will explore the future of funeral practices and how they may continue to evolve in the coming years.

#### The Rise of Green Funerals

One of the emerging trends in funeral practices is the rise of green funerals. Green funerals, also known as eco-funerals, aim to minimize the environmental impact of funeral services. This includes using natural and biodegradable materials, reducing energy consumption, and promoting sustainable practices. The concept of green funerals aligns with the growing global movement towards sustainability and environmental responsibility.

#### The Role of Technology in Funeral Practices

Technology has already played a significant role in the funeral industry, with the rise of online funeral planning and memorial websites. In the future, we can expect to see even more advancements in technology, such as virtual reality mourning experiences and 3D printing of funeral urns. These advancements may also lead to more personalized and interactive funeral services, allowing families to create unique and meaningful tributes to their loved ones.

#### The Impact of Changing Demographics

As the demographics of the United States continue to change, so will the funeral practices of the nation. With the increasing diversity of the population, we may see a rise in traditional funeral practices from different cultures and religions. This could include the incorporation of rituals and customs from various cultures into funeral services, reflecting the changing demographics of the country.

#### The Future of Cremation

Cremation has already become a popular alternative to traditional burial, and it is expected to continue to grow in the future. With the rise of green funerals and the increasing acceptance of cremation, we may see a shift towards more sustainable and environmentally friendly funeral practices. This could include the use of natural and biodegradable materials for cremation, as well as the promotion of green burial options.

#### The Impact of Changing Attitudes towards Death

As our society continues to evolve, so will our attitudes towards death and dying. With the rise of the death positivity movement and the increasing acceptance of death as a natural part of life, we may see a shift towards more personalized and meaningful funeral practices. This could include the incorporation of personal rituals and traditions into funeral services, as well as a focus on celebrating the life of the deceased rather than mourning their death.

In conclusion, the future of funeral practices is constantly evolving, shaped by cultural, religious, and societal influences. As we continue to adapt and evolve as a society, so will our funeral practices, reflecting our changing values and beliefs. The rise of green funerals, the role of technology, changing demographics, the future of cremation, and changing attitudes towards death are just some of the factors that will continue to shape the future of funeral practices in the United States.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the history and evolution of cemeteries in American urban areas. From the early days of burial grounds and graveyards to the modern-day cemeteries, we have seen how these spaces have transformed over time. We have also delved into the various cultural and religious influences that have shaped the design and practices of cemeteries, as well as the social and economic factors that have played a role in their development.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of cemeteries in our society. They serve as a reminder of our mortality and a place for us to mourn and remember our loved ones. Cemeteries also play a crucial role in preserving our history and cultural heritage, as they often contain the final resting places of prominent figures and important historical artifacts.

As we continue to grow and evolve as a society, it is important to consider the future of cemeteries. With the increasing urbanization and limited space, we may see a shift towards more modern and innovative cemetery designs. We may also see a rise in the use of green burials and other sustainable practices in the funeral industry.

This phenomenon has been occurring in the United States since the early 19th century, and it has had a profound impact on the country's social, economic, and political landscape.

The United States is often referred to as a "nation of cities," and for good reason. According to the United States Census Bureau, as of 2019, 81.6% of the US population lives in urban areas. This is a significant increase from just over 50% in 1900. The growth of urban areas in the United States has been driven by a variety of factors, including economic opportunities, technological advancements, and social and cultural changes.

In this chapter, we will explore the history of urbanization in the United States, from its early beginnings to the present day. ## Chapter: American Urban History II: Exploring the Growth of American Cities

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the topic of urbanization in the United States. Urbanization is the process of migration from rural to urban areas, resulting in the growth of cities and their populations. This phenomenon has been occurring in the United States since the early 19th century, and it has had a significant impact on the country's social, economic, and political landscape.

The United States is known for its diverse and complex urban landscape, with a wide range of cities varying in size, culture, and development. From the bustling streets of New York City to the quaint charm of small towns, the urban landscape of the United States is constantly evolving. In this chapter, we will explore the factors that have contributed to this growth, as well as the challenges and opportunities that come with it.

We will also examine the history of urbanization in the United States, from its early beginnings to the present day. This will include a discussion of the various factors that have influenced urbanization, such as economic opportunities, transportation, and social and cultural factors. We will also explore the impact of urbanization on different communities and how it has shaped the country's social and economic fabric.

Furthermore, we will discuss the current state of urbanization in the United States and the future prospects for its growth. This will include a look at the challenges facing urban areas, such as gentrification, inequality, and sustainability, as well as potential solutions and strategies for addressing these issues.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of urbanization in the United States, its history, and its impact on the country. By exploring the growth of American cities, we can gain valuable insights into the complex and ever-changing urban landscape of the United States. 


## Chapter 1:3: Urbanization:




### Subsection: 12.2a Challenges Facing Urban Areas

As we have seen throughout this book, the growth of American cities has been a complex and dynamic process, shaped by a multitude of factors and influences. However, as cities continue to grow and evolve, they face a number of challenges that must be addressed in order to ensure their sustainability and livability. In this section, we will explore some of the key challenges facing urban areas in the United States.

#### Urbanization and Population Growth

One of the most significant challenges facing urban areas is the rapid pace of urbanization and population growth. According to the United Nations, by 2050, 68% of the world's population is expected to live in urban areas. In the United States, this trend is already evident, with 81% of the population living in urban areas as of 2019. This rapid growth puts pressure on existing infrastructure and resources, and can lead to issues such as overcrowding, inadequate housing, and strain on public services.

#### Inequality and Discrimination

Another major challenge facing urban areas is the issue of inequality and discrimination. As cities become more diverse, it is essential to create inclusive and equitable environments for all residents. However, discrimination and exclusion persist in many urban areas, leading to unequal access to opportunities and resources. This can have a significant impact on the well-being and quality of life of marginalized communities.

#### Environmental Challenges

The growth of urban areas also brings with it a range of environmental challenges. Urbanization can lead to increased pollution, energy consumption, and waste generation. This can have negative impacts on the surrounding environment and ecosystems. Additionally, the urban heat island effect, where urban areas are significantly warmer than surrounding rural areas, can exacerbate the effects of climate change and contribute to extreme heat events.

#### Smart City Challenges

While the concept of smart cities offers potential solutions to some of these challenges, there are also challenges associated with implementing and maintaining smart city technologies. These include issues of privacy and security, as well as the potential for unequal access to technology and its benefits. Additionally, the rapid pace of technological advancements can make it difficult for cities to keep up and effectively utilize these technologies.

#### Future Challenges

As we look towards the future, it is important to consider the potential challenges that may arise as cities continue to grow and evolve. These may include the need for more sustainable and resilient infrastructure, the impact of emerging technologies on urban life, and the potential for increased social and economic inequalities. It is crucial for urban planners and policymakers to address these challenges proactively in order to create livable and sustainable cities for all.





### Subsection: 12.2b Urban Resilience and Sustainability

As we have seen in the previous section, urban areas face a range of challenges that must be addressed in order to ensure their sustainability and livability. In this section, we will explore some of the key strategies and initiatives that have been implemented to address these challenges and promote urban resilience and sustainability.

#### Smart City Initiatives

One of the key strategies for promoting urban resilience and sustainability is through the implementation of smart city initiatives. These initiatives aim to use technology and data to improve the efficiency and sustainability of urban systems, such as transportation, energy, and waste management. For example, the use of self-healing technology can reduce maintenance and improve the sustainability of urban developments, while the implementation of renewable energy sources can reduce energy consumption and improve the reliability and security of urban systems.

#### Urban Planning and Design

Urban planning and design also play a crucial role in promoting urban resilience and sustainability. By considering the long-term impacts of urban development, planners and designers can create more sustainable and resilient cities. This can include incorporating green spaces and natural systems into urban design, promoting mixed-use development to reduce the need for transportation, and designing buildings and infrastructure to withstand extreme weather events.

#### Community Engagement and Participation

Engaging and involving the community in urban planning and decision-making processes is essential for promoting urban resilience and sustainability. By involving community members in the planning and design of their cities, their needs and concerns can be addressed, and they can take ownership of their urban environment. This can also lead to a sense of community pride and a stronger sense of belonging, which can contribute to the overall livability and sustainability of urban areas.

#### Policy and Regulation

Policy and regulation also play a crucial role in promoting urban resilience and sustainability. By implementing policies and regulations that prioritize sustainability and resilience, cities can incentivize developers and residents to make more environmentally friendly and resilient choices. This can include policies that promote the use of renewable energy sources, regulations that require green building practices, and incentives for residents to reduce their energy consumption.

#### Collaboration and Partnerships

Collaboration and partnerships between different stakeholders, such as government agencies, businesses, and community organizations, are also essential for promoting urban resilience and sustainability. By working together, these stakeholders can share resources, knowledge, and expertise to address complex urban challenges and implement innovative solutions. This can also lead to a more holistic and comprehensive approach to urban development, rather than addressing issues in isolation.

In conclusion, promoting urban resilience and sustainability requires a multifaceted approach that considers the interconnectedness of urban systems and the needs and concerns of all stakeholders. By implementing smart city initiatives, incorporating sustainable urban planning and design, engaging the community, and promoting collaboration and partnerships, we can create more resilient and sustainable cities for the future.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the growth of American cities and the various factors that have contributed to their development. From the early settlements of indigenous peoples to the modern metropolises of today, the history of urbanization in America is a complex and ever-evolving story.

We have seen how the arrival of European colonizers and the introduction of slavery shaped the early cities of America, and how the Industrial Revolution brought about a rapid transformation in urban life. We have also examined the impact of immigration and migration on the growth of cities, as well as the role of government policies and urban planning in shaping the built environment.

Furthermore, we have delved into the social, economic, and cultural aspects of urban life, exploring the challenges and opportunities that come with living in a city. From the rise of urban poverty and inequality to the emergence of vibrant cultural scenes, the urban experience in America is a diverse and dynamic one.

As we conclude this book, it is important to recognize that the history of urbanization in America is not just a story of the past, but also a story of the present and future. The challenges and opportunities that we face in our cities today are a direct result of the decisions and actions of past generations, and it is up to us to shape the future of our urban spaces.

## Chapter: American Urban History II: Exploring the Growth of American Cities

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the topic of urbanization in America. Urbanization is the process of migration from rural areas to cities, resulting in the growth of urban populations. This phenomenon has been occurring in America since the early 19th century, and it has had a significant impact on the development of the country. In this chapter, we will explore the various factors that have contributed to urbanization in America, including economic, social, and political factors. We will also examine the effects of urbanization on the urban landscape and the lives of urban dwellers. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the complex and ever-evolving nature of urbanization in America.


# American Urban History II: Exploring the Growth of American Cities

## Chapter 13: Urbanization




### Subsection: 12.2c Future Directions in Urban Studies

As we have seen in the previous sections, urban areas face a range of challenges that must be addressed in order to ensure their sustainability and livability. In this section, we will explore some of the key areas of research that are emerging in the field of urban studies.

#### Urban Informatics

Urban informatics is a rapidly growing field that combines urban planning, information technology, and data analysis to improve the efficiency and sustainability of urban systems. This field is particularly interested in the use of data and technology to address urban challenges, such as traffic congestion, energy consumption, and waste management. For example, urban informatics researchers are exploring the use of real-time data and predictive analytics to optimize traffic flow and reduce congestion, as well as the use of smart sensors and data analytics to improve energy efficiency in buildings.

#### Urban Ecology

Urban ecology is a field that focuses on the study of urban ecosystems and their impact on human health and well-being. This field is particularly interested in understanding the complex interactions between urban environments and human health, and how urban development can impact the health of both individuals and communities. For example, urban ecologists are studying the effects of urban heat islands on human health, as well as the impact of urban air pollution on respiratory and cardiovascular health.

#### Urban Resilience

Urban resilience is a concept that refers to the ability of a city to withstand and recover from shocks and stresses, such as natural disasters, economic downturns, or social unrest. This field is particularly interested in understanding the factors that contribute to urban resilience, as well as the strategies and policies that can be used to promote resilience in urban areas. For example, urban resilience researchers are studying the role of social networks and community cohesion in promoting resilience, as well as the use of green infrastructure and natural systems to enhance resilience.

#### Urban Computing

Urban computing is a field that focuses on the use of computational methods and technologies to understand and improve urban environments. This field is particularly interested in the use of data and algorithms to analyze and optimize urban systems, such as transportation, energy, and waste management. For example, urban computing researchers are exploring the use of machine learning and artificial intelligence to improve traffic flow, reduce energy consumption, and optimize waste collection.

#### Urban Design and Planning

Urban design and planning is a field that focuses on the design and management of urban environments to create livable, sustainable, and equitable cities. This field is particularly interested in understanding the complex interactions between urban design, planning, and human behavior, and how these factors can impact the livability and sustainability of urban areas. For example, urban design and planning researchers are studying the effects of urban design on pedestrian and bicycle mobility, as well as the impact of urban planning policies on housing affordability and social equity.
